Proof:

After renaming modulo the bijection { a ↦ 0, c ↦ 1, b ↦ 2 },
  it remains to prove termination of the 6-rules system (4 strict rules)
{ 0 1 2 ⟶ 2 2 0 ,
  0 1 2 ⟶ 0 1 1 ,
  2 2 2 ⟶ 0 0 1 ,
  1 0 1 ⟶ 2 2 2 ,
  2 0 2 →= 2 0 2 ,
  2 0 0 →= 2 0 2 }

Removing trivial non-strict rules.
After renaming modulo the bijection { 0 ↦ 0, 1 ↦ 1, 2 ↦ 2 },
  it remains to prove termination of the 5-rules system (4 strict rules)
{ 0 1 2 ⟶ 2 2 0 ,
  0 1 2 ⟶ 0 1 1 ,
  2 2 2 ⟶ 0 0 1 ,
  1 0 1 ⟶ 2 2 2 ,
  2 0 0 →= 2 0 2 }

Strictifying the system, i. e., replacing each non-strict rule l →= r by l → r.

After renaming modulo the bijection { 0 ↦ 0, 1 ↦ 1, 2 ↦ 2 },
  it remains to prove termination of the 5-rules system (5 strict rules)
{ 0 1 2 ⟶ 2 2 0 ,
  0 1 2 ⟶ 0 1 1 ,
  2 2 2 ⟶ 0 0 1 ,
  1 0 1 ⟶ 2 2 2 ,
  2 0 0 ⟶ 2 0 2 }

Reversing the system.
After renaming modulo the bijection { 2 ↦ 0, 1 ↦ 1, 0 ↦ 2 },
  it remains to prove termination of the 5-rules system (5 strict rules)
{ 0 1 2 ⟶ 2 0 0 ,
  0 1 2 ⟶ 1 1 2 ,
  0 0 0 ⟶ 1 2 2 ,
  1 2 1 ⟶ 0 0 0 ,
  2 2 0 ⟶ 0 2 0 }

Applying the dependency pairs transformation [Arts, CAAP 1996], [Arts/Giesl, RTA 1996].
  Here, ↑ marks so-called defined symbols.
After renaming modulo the bijection { (0,↑) ↦ 0, (1,↓) ↦ 1, (2,↓) ↦ 2, (2,↑) ↦ 3, (0,↓) ↦ 4, (1,↑) ↦ 5 },
  it remains to prove termination of the 16-rules system (11 strict rules)
{ 0 1 2 ⟶ 3 4 4 ,
  0 1 2 ⟶ 0 4 ,
  0 1 2 ⟶ 0 ,
  0 1 2 ⟶ 5 1 2 ,
  0 4 4 ⟶ 5 2 2 ,
  0 4 4 ⟶ 3 2 ,
  0 4 4 ⟶ 3 ,
  5 2 1 ⟶ 0 4 4 ,
  5 2 1 ⟶ 0 4 ,
  5 2 1 ⟶ 0 ,
  3 2 4 ⟶ 0 2 4 ,
  4 1 2 →= 2 4 4 ,
  4 1 2 →= 1 1 2 ,
  4 4 4 →= 1 2 2 ,
  1 2 1 →= 4 4 4 ,
  2 2 4 →= 4 2 4 }
